<div class="plainlist">
<ul>
<li>Go Further</li>
<li>Built Ford Tough</li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;">Website</th>
<td style="line-height:1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ford.com/">www<wbr />.ford<wbr />.com</a></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Ford Motor Company</b> (commonly referred to as simply <b>Ford</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> automaker headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Dearborn,_Michigan" title="Dearborn, Michigan">Dearborn, Michigan</a>, a suburb of <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>. It was founded by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">Henry Ford</a> and incorporated on June 16, 1903. The company sells automobiles and commercial vehicles under the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ford_vehicles" title="List of Ford vehicles">Ford</a> brand and most luxury cars under the <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Motor_Company" title="Lincoln Motor Company">Lincoln</a> brand. Ford also owns Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUV</a> manufacturer, <a href="/wiki/Troller" title="Troller" class="mw-redirect">Troller</a>, and Australian performance car manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Ford_Performance_Vehicles" title="Ford Performance Vehicles">FPV</a>. In the past it has also produced tractors and automotive components. Ford owns a 2.1% stake in <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> of Japan, an 8% stake in <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a> of the United Kingdom, and a 49% stake in <a href="/wiki/Jiangling_Motors" title="Jiangling Motors">Jiangling</a> of China. It also has a number of joint-ventures, two in China (<a href="/wiki/Changan_Ford_Mazda" title="Changan Ford Mazda">Changan Ford Mazda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Lio_Ho" title="Ford Lio Ho" class="mw-redirect">Ford Lio Ho</a>), one in Thailand (<a href="/wiki/AutoAlliance_Thailand" title="AutoAlliance Thailand">AutoAlliance Thailand</a>), one in Turkey (<a href="/wiki/Ford_Otosan" title="Ford Otosan">Ford Otosan</a>), and one in Russia (<a href="/wiki/Ford_Sollers" title="Ford Sollers">Ford Sollers</a>). It is listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> and is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Ford_family_tree" title="Ford family tree">Ford family</a>, although they have minority ownership.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ford introduced methods for large-scale manufacturing of cars and large-scale management of an industrial workforce using elaborately engineered manufacturing sequences typified by moving <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly lines</a>; by 1914 these methods were known around the world as <a href="/wiki/Fordism" title="Fordism">Fordism</a>. Ford's former UK subsidiaries <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a>, acquired in 1989 and 2000 respectively, were sold to <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> in March 2008. Ford owned the Swedish automaker <a href="/wiki/Volvo_cars" title="Volvo cars" class="mw-redirect">Volvo</a> from 1999 to 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, Ford discontinued the <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(automobile)" title="Mercury (automobile)">Mercury</a> brand, under which it had marketed entry-level luxury cars in the United States, Canada, Mexico, and the Middle East since 1938.</p>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">the financial crisis</a> at the beginning of the 21st century, it was close to bankruptcy, but it has since returned to profitability.</p>
<p>Ford is the second-largest U.S.-based automaker (preceded by <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry#By_manufacturer" title="Automotive industry">fifth-largest</a> in the world based on 2010 vehicle sales.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> At the end of 2010, Ford was the fifth largest automaker in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford is the eighth-ranked overall American-based company in the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list, based on global revenues in 2009 of $118.3&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, Ford produced 5.532&#160;million automobiles<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> and employed about 213,000 employees at around 90 plants and facilities worldwide.</p>
<p>The company went public in 1956 but the Ford family, through special Class B shares, still retain 40 percent voting rights.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ford_Motor_Company" title="History of Ford Motor Company">History of Ford Motor Company</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_ford_1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Henry_ford_1919.jpg/170px-Henry_ford_1919.jpg" width="170" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Henry_ford_1919.jpg/255px-Henry_ford_1919.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Henry_ford_1919.jpg/340px-Henry_ford_1919.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1744" data-file-height="2226" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1910Ford-T.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1910Ford-T.jpg/220px-1910Ford-T.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1910Ford-T.jpg/330px-1910Ford-T.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/1910Ford-T.jpg/440px-1910Ford-T.jpg 2x" data-file-width="670" data-file-height="527" /></a>

</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3>
<p>Henry Ford's first attempt at a car company under his own name was the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford_Company" title="Henry Ford Company">Henry Ford Company</a> on November 3, 1901, which became the <a href="/wiki/Cadillac_Motor_Company" title="Cadillac Motor Company" class="mw-redirect">Cadillac Motor Company</a> on August 22, 1902, after Ford left with the rights to his name. The Ford Motor Company was launched in a converted factory in 1903 with $28,000 in cash from twelve investors, most notably <a href="/wiki/John_Francis_Dodge" title="John Francis Dodge">John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horace_Elgin_Dodge" title="Horace Elgin Dodge">Horace Dodge</a> (who would later found <a href="/wiki/Dodge_Brothers_Motor_Vehicle_Company" title="Dodge Brothers Motor Vehicle Company" class="mw-redirect">their own</a> car company). During its early years, the company produced just a few cars a day at its factory on Mack Avenue and later its <a href="/wiki/Ford_Piquette_Avenue_Plant" title="Ford Piquette Avenue Plant">factory on Piquette Avenue</a> in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>. Groups of two or three men worked on each car, assembling it from parts made mostly by supplier companies contracting for Ford. Within a decade the company would lead the world in the expansion and refinement of the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly line</a> concept; and Ford soon brought much of the part production in-house in a <a href="/wiki/Vertical_integration" title="Vertical integration">vertical integration</a> that seemed a better path for the era.</p>
<p>Henry Ford was 39 years old when he founded the Ford Motor Company, which would go on to become one of the world's largest and most profitable companies. As one of the largest family-controlled companies in the world, the Ford Motor Company has been in continuous family control for over 100 years.</p>
<p>After the first gasoline powered <a href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile" class="mw-redirect">automobile</a> was created in the year 1885 by <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> inventor <a href="/wiki/Karl_Benz" title="Karl Benz">Carl Benz</a> (<a href="/wiki/Benz_Patent-Motorwagen" title="Benz Patent-Motorwagen">Benz Patent-Motorwagen</a>), more efficient production methods were needed to make the automobile affordable for the middle-class; which Ford contributed to, for instance by introducing the first moving <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly line</a> in 1913 at its <a href="/wiki/Highland_Park_Ford_Plant" title="Highland Park Ford Plant">factory in Highland Park</a>.</p>
<p>Between 1903 and 1908 Ford produced the Models A, B, C, F, K, N, R, and S, most of which sold in the hundreds or few thousands a year. In 1908 Ford introduced the mass-produced <a href="/wiki/Model_T" title="Model T" class="mw-redirect">Model T</a>, which would sell in the millions. In 1927, Ford replaced the T with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Model_A_(1927%E2%80%931931)" title="Ford Model A (1927–1931)" class="mw-redirect">Model A</a>, the first car with safety glass in the windshield.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford launched the first low priced V8 engine powered car in 1932.</p>
<p>The creation of a scientific laboratory in Dearborn, Michigan in 1951, doing unfettered basic research, led to Ford's unlikely involvement in <a href="/wiki/Superconductivity" title="Superconductivity">superconductivity</a> research. In 1964 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ford_Research_Labs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ford Research Labs (page does not exist)">Ford Research Labs</a> made a key breakthrough with the invention of a superconducting quantum interference device or <a href="/wiki/SQUID" title="SQUID">SQUID</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ford offered the Lifeguard safety package from 1956, which included such innovations as a standard deep-dish steering wheel, optional front, and, for the first time in a car, rear seatbelts, and an optional padded dash.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford introduced child-proof door locks into its products in 1957, and in the same year offered the first retractable hardtop on a mass-produced six-seater car. The Ford Mustang was introduced in 1964. In 1965 Ford introduced the seat belt reminder light.</p>
<p>With the 1980s, Ford introduced several highly successful vehicles around the world. During the 1980s, Ford began using the advertising slogan, "Have you driven a Ford, lately?" to introduce new customers to their brand and make their vehicles appear more modern. In 1990 and 1994 respectively, Ford also acquired <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar Cars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> During the mid- to late 1990s, Ford continued to sell large numbers of vehicles, in a booming <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> economy with a soaring stock market and low fuel prices.</p>
<p>With the dawn of the new century, legacy healthcare costs, higher fuel prices, and a faltering economy led to falling market shares, declining sales, and diminished profit margins. Most of the corporate profits came from financing consumer automobile loans through <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Credit_Company" title="Ford Motor Credit Company">Ford Motor Credit Company</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Ford_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bill_Ford_2011.jpg/180px-Bill_Ford_2011.jpg" width="180" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bill_Ford_2011.jpg/270px-Bill_Ford_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bill_Ford_2011.jpg/360px-Bill_Ford_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2492" data-file-height="3502" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Ford_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/William_Clay_Ford,_Jr." title="William Clay Ford, Jr.">William Clay Ford, Jr.</a>, great-grandson of Henry Ford, serves as the <a href="/wiki/Executive_chairman" title="Executive chairman" class="mw-redirect">executive chairman</a> at the board of Ford Motor Company.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By 2005, both Ford and <a href="/wiki/General_motors" title="General motors" class="mw-redirect">GM</a>'s corporate bonds had been downgraded to junk status,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> as a result of high U.S. health care costs for an <a href="/wiki/Aging_in_the_American_workforce" title="Aging in the American workforce">aging workforce</a>, soaring gasoline prices, eroding market share, and an over dependence on declining <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUV</a> sales. Profit margins decreased on large vehicles due to increased "incentives" (in the form of rebates or low interest financing) to offset declining demand.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> In the latter half of 2005, Chairman Bill Ford asked newly appointed Ford Americas Division President <a href="/wiki/Mark_Fields_(businessman)" title="Mark Fields (businessman)">Mark Fields</a> to develop a plan to return the company to profitability. Fields previewed the Plan, named <i><a href="/wiki/The_Way_Forward" title="The Way Forward">The Way Forward</a></i>, at the December 7, 2005 board meeting of the company and it was unveiled to the public on January 23, 2006. "The Way Forward" included resizing the company to match market realities, dropping some unprofitable and inefficient models, consolidating production lines, closing 14 factories and cutting 30,000 jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ford moved to introduce a range of new vehicles, including "<a href="/wiki/Crossover_SUV" title="Crossover SUV" class="mw-redirect">Crossover SUVs</a>" built on <a href="/wiki/Unibody" title="Unibody" class="mw-redirect">unibody</a> car platforms, rather than more <a href="/wiki/Body-on-frame" title="Body-on-frame">body-on-frame</a> chassis. In developing the hybrid electric powertrain technologies for the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape Hybrid</a> SUV, Ford licensed similar Toyota hybrid technologies<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> to avoid patent infringements.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford announced that it will team up with electricity supply company <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Edison" title="Southern California Edison">Southern California Edison</a> (SCE) to examine the future of <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">plug-in hybrids</a> in terms of how home and vehicle energy systems will work with the electrical grid. Under the multimillion-dollar, multi-year project, Ford will convert a demonstration fleet of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escape_Hybrid" title="Ford Escape Hybrid" class="mw-redirect">Ford Escape Hybrids</a> into plug-in hybrids, and SCE will evaluate how the vehicles might interact with the home and the utility's electrical grid. Some of the vehicles will be evaluated "in typical customer settings", according to Ford.<sup id="cite_ref-akhrum_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-akhrum-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-edison_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edison-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/William_Clay_Ford_Jr." title="William Clay Ford Jr." class="mw-redirect">William Clay Ford Jr.</a>, great-grandson of Henry Ford (and better known by his nickname "Bill"), was appointed Executive Chairman in 1998, and also became Chief Executive Officer of the company in 2001, with the departure of <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Nasser" title="Jacques Nasser">Jacques Nasser</a>, becoming the first member of the Ford family to head the company since the retirement of his uncle, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford_II" title="Henry Ford II">Henry Ford II</a>, in 1982. Upon the retirement of President and Chief Operation Officer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Padilla" title="Jim Padilla">Jim Padilla</a> in April 2006, Bill Ford assumed his roles as well. Five months later, in September, Ford named <a href="/wiki/Alan_Mulally" title="Alan Mulally">Alan Mulally</a> as President and CEO, with Ford continuing as Executive Chairman. In December 2006, the company raised its borrowing capacity to about $25&#160;billion, placing substantially all corporate assets as collateral.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Chairman Bill Ford has stated that "bankruptcy is not an option".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford and the <a href="/wiki/United_Auto_Workers" title="United Auto Workers" class="mw-redirect">United Auto Workers</a>, representing approximately 46,000 hourly workers in North America, agreed to a historic contract settlement in November 2007 giving the company a substantial break in terms of its ongoing retiree health care costs and other economic issues. The agreement included the establishment of a company-funded, independently run <a href="/wiki/Voluntary_Employee_Beneficiary_Association" title="Voluntary Employee Beneficiary Association">Voluntary Employee Beneficiary Association</a> (VEBA) trust to shift the burden of retiree health care from the company's books, thereby improving its balance sheet. This arrangement took effect on January 1, 2010. As a sign of its currently strong cash position, Ford contributed its entire current liability (estimated at approximately <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$5.5&#160;billion</span> as of December 31, 2009) to the VEBA in cash, and also pre-paid <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$500&#160;million</span> of its future liabilities to the fund. The agreement also gives hourly workers the job security they were seeking by having the company commit to substantial investments in most of its factories.</p>
<p>The automaker reported the largest annual loss in company history in 2006 of $12.7&#160;billion,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> and estimated that it would not return to profitability until 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> However, Ford surprised <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a> in the second quarter of 2007 by posting a $750&#160;million profit. Despite the gains, the company finished the year with a $2.7&#160;billion loss, largely attributed to finance restructuring at <a href="/wiki/Volvo_cars" title="Volvo cars" class="mw-redirect">Volvo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On June 2, 2008, Ford sold its Jaguar and Land Rover operations to <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> for $2.3&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-r_20080602_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r_20080602-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During Congressional hearings held in November 2008 at Washington D.C., and in a show of support, Ford's Alan Mulally stated that "We at Ford are hopeful that we have enough liquidity. But we also must prepare ourselves for the prospect of further deteriorating economic conditions". Mulally went on to state that "The collapse of one of our competitors would have a severe impact on Ford" and that Ford Motor Company's supports both Chrysler and General Motors in their search for government bridge loans in the face of conditions caused by the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932012_global_financial_crisis" title="2007–2012 global financial crisis" class="mw-redirect">2008 financial crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Together, the three companies presented action plans for the sustainability of the industry. Mulally stated that "In addition to our plan, we are also here today to request support for the industry. In the near-term, Ford does not require access to a government bridge loan. However, we request a credit line of $9 billion as a critical backstop or safeguard against worsening conditions as we drive transformational change in our company" <sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> GM and Chrysler received government loans and financing through <a href="/wiki/T.A.R.P." title="T.A.R.P." class="mw-redirect">T.A.R.P.</a> legislation funding provisions.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On December 19, the cost of <a href="/wiki/Credit_default_swap" title="Credit default swap">credit default swaps</a> to insure the debt of Ford was 68 percent the sum insured for five years in addition to annual payments of 5 percent. That meant $6.8&#160;million paid upfront to insure $10&#160;million in debt, in addition to payments of $500,000 per year.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> In January 2009, Ford reported a $14.6&#160;billion loss in the preceding year, a record for the company. The company retained sufficient liquidity to fund its operations. Through April 2009, Ford's strategy of debt for equity exchanges erased $9.9 billion in liabilities (28% of its total) in order to leverage its cash position.<sup id="cite_ref-Dolan_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dolan-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> These actions yielded Ford a $2.7&#160;billion profit in fiscal year 2009, the company's first full-year profit in four years.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, Ford's corporate bonds were upgraded from junk to investment grade again, citing sustainable, lasting improvements.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On October 29, 2012, Ford announced the sale of its climate control components business, its last remaining automotive components operation, to Detroit Thermal Systems LLC for an undisclosed price.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On November 1, 2012, Ford announced that <a href="/wiki/CEO" title="CEO" class="mw-redirect">CEO</a> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Mulally" title="Alan Mulally">Alan Mulally</a> will stay with the company until 2014. Ford also named <a href="/wiki/Mark_Fields_(businessman)" title="Mark Fields (businessman)">Mark Fields</a>, the president of operations in Americas, as its new chief operating officer <sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford's CEO Mulally was paid a compensation of over $174 million in his previous seven years at Ford since 2006. The generous amount has been a sore point for some workers of the company.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_management">Executive management</span></h3>
<p>Members of the Ford board as of July 2014 are: <a href="/wiki/Dick_Gephardt" title="Dick Gephardt">Richard A. Gephardt</a>, Stephen Butler, Ellen Marram, <a href="/wiki/Kimberly_Casiano" title="Kimberly Casiano">Kimberly Casiano</a>, Mark Fields (President and CEO), <a href="/wiki/Edsel_Ford_II" title="Edsel Ford II">Edsel Ford II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homer_Neal" title="Homer Neal">Homer Neal</a>, William Clay Ford Jr. (Executive Chairman), Anthony F. Earley, Jr., James P. Hackett, <a href="/wiki/John_L._Thornton" title="John L. Thornton">John L. Thornton</a>, James H. Hance, Jr., William W. Helman IV, Jon M. Huntsman, Jr., John C. Lechleiter and Gerald L. Shaheen.<sup id="cite_ref-fmci_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fmci-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_results">Financial results</span></h3>
<p>In 2010, Ford earned a net profit of $6.6&#160;billion and reduced its debt from $33.6&#160;billion to $14.5&#160;billion lowering interest payments by $1&#160;billion following its 2009 net profit of $2.7&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-2010results_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010results-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-annualreport2009_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annualreport2009-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> In the U.S., the F-Series was the best-selling vehicle for 2010. Ford sold 528,349 F-Series trucks during the year, a 27.7% increase over 2009, out of a total sales of 1.9&#160;million vehicles, or every one out of four vehicles Ford sold. Trucks sales accounts for a big slice of Ford's profits, according to USA Today.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford's realignment also included the sale of its wholly owned subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/The_Hertz_Corporation" title="The Hertz Corporation">Hertz Rent-a-Car</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Private_equity" title="Private equity">private equity</a> group for $15&#160;billion in cash and debt acquisition. The sale was completed on December 22, 2005. A 50–50 joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Mahindra_%26_Mahindra" title="Mahindra &amp; Mahindra">Mahindra &amp; Mahindra</a> of India, called <a href="/wiki/Ford_India_Private_Limited" title="Ford India Private Limited">Mahindra Ford India, Limited</a> (MIFL), ended with Ford buying out Mahindra's remaining stake in the company in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford had previously upped its stake to 72% in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span></h2>
<p>Ford has manufacturing <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ford_factories" title="List of Ford factories">operations</a> worldwide, including in the United States, Canada, Mexico, China, the United Kingdom, Germany, Turkey, Brazil, Argentina, Australia and South Africa. Ford also has a cooperative agreement with Russian automaker <a href="/wiki/GAZ" title="GAZ">GAZ</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike,_Mineola,_Garden_City.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike%2C_Mineola%2C_Garden_City.jpg/220px-The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike%2C_Mineola%2C_Garden_City.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike%2C_Mineola%2C_Garden_City.jpg/330px-The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike%2C_Mineola%2C_Garden_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike%2C_Mineola%2C_Garden_City.jpg/440px-The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike%2C_Mineola%2C_Garden_City.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1453" data-file-height="909" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Ford_building_--_Jericho_Turnpike,_Mineola,_Garden_City.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ford dealer in <a href="/wiki/Garden_City,_New_York" title="Garden City, New York">Garden City, New York</a>, ca. 1930–1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the first five months of 2010, auto sales in the U.S. rose to 4.6&#160;million cars and light trucks, an increase of 17% from a year earlier. The rise was mainly caused by the return of commercial customers that had all but stopped buying in 2009 during the recession. Sales to individual customers at dealerships have increased 13%, while fleet sales have jumped 32%.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford reported that 37% of its sales in May came from fleet sales when it announced its sales for the month increased 23%.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> In the first seven months of 2010, vehicle sales of Ford increased 24%, including retail and fleet sales. Fleet sales of Ford for the same period rose 35% to 386,000 units while retail sales increase 19%. Fleet sales account for 39 percent of Chrysler's sales and 31 percent for GM's.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ford_of_Europe" title="Ford of Europe">Ford of Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg/220px-Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg/330px-Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg/440px-Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford%27s_Dunton_Technical_Centre_-_geograph.org.uk_-_218069.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ford's <a href="/wiki/Dunton_Technical_Centre" title="Dunton Technical Centre">Dunton Technical Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Laindon" title="Laindon">Laindon</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, the largest automotive research and development facility in the country<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg/220px-Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg/330px-Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg/440px-Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1176" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aachen_Ford-Entwicklungszentrum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Ford Research Center in <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At first, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Germany" title="Ford Germany">Ford in Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_of_Britain" title="Ford of Britain">Ford in Britain</a> built different models from one another until the late 1960s, with the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_(Europe)" title="Ford Escort (Europe)">Ford Escort</a> and then the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Capri" title="Ford Capri">Ford Capri</a> being common to both companies. Later on, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Taunus" title="Ford Taunus">Ford Taunus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cortina" title="Ford Cortina">Ford Cortina</a> became identical, produced in <a href="/wiki/Left_hand_drive" title="Left hand drive" class="mw-redirect">left hand drive</a> and right hand drive respectively. Rationalisation of model ranges meant that production of many models in the UK switched to elsewhere in Europe, including Belgium and Spain as well as Germany. The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Ford Sierra</a> replaced the Taunus and Cortina in 1982, drawing criticism for its radical aerodynamic styling, which was soon given nicknames such as "Jellymould" and "The Salesman's Spaceship."</p>
<p>Increasingly, the Ford Motor Company has looked to <a href="/wiki/Ford_Europe" title="Ford Europe" class="mw-redirect">Ford of Europe</a> for its "world cars", such as the Mondeo, Focus, and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Fiesta</a>, although sales of European-sourced Fords in the U.S. have been disappointing. The Focus has been one exception to this, which has become America's best selling compact car since its launch in 2000.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In February 2002, Ford ended car production in the UK. It was the first time in 90 years that Ford cars had not been made in Britain, although production of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit" title="Ford Transit">Transit</a> van continued at the company's <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a> facility until mid-2013, engines at <a href="/wiki/Bridgend" title="Bridgend">Bridgend</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Dagenham" title="Ford Dagenham">Dagenham</a>, and transmissions at <a href="/wiki/Halewood" title="Halewood">Halewood</a>. Development of European Ford is broadly split between <a href="/wiki/Dunton_Wayletts" title="Dunton Wayletts">Dunton</a> in Essex (powertrain, Fiesta/Ka, and commercial vehicles) and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> (body, chassis, electrical, Focus, Mondeo) in Germany. Ford also produced the <a href="/wiki/Thames_Trader" title="Thames Trader">Thames</a> range of commercial vehicles, although the use of this brand name was discontinued circa 1965. Elsewhere in continental Europe, Ford assembles the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Mondeo</a> range in <a href="/wiki/Genk" title="Genk">Genk</a> (Belgium), Fiesta in <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a> (Spain) and <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> (Germany), Ka in Valencia (Spain), Focus in Valencia (Spain), <a href="/wiki/Saarlouis" title="Saarlouis">Saarlouis</a> (Germany) and <a href="/wiki/Vsevolozhsk" title="Vsevolozhsk">Vsevolozhsk</a> (Russia). Transit production is in <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmit" title="İzmit">Kocaeli</a> (Turkey), <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a> (UK), and Transit Connect in <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmit" title="İzmit">Kocaeli</a> (Turkey).</p>
<p>Ford also owns a joint-venture production plant in Turkey. <a href="/wiki/Otosan" title="Otosan" class="mw-redirect">Ford Otosan</a>, established in the 1970s, manufactures the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Connect" title="Ford Transit Connect">Transit Connect</a> compact panel van as well as the "Jumbo" and long-wheelbase versions of the full-size Transit. This new production facility was set up near <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmit" title="İzmit">Kocaeli</a> in 2002, and its opening marked the end of Transit assembly in Genk.</p>
<p>Another joint venture plant near <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal" title="Setúbal">Setúbal</a> in Portugal, set up in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>, formerly assembled the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Galaxy" title="Ford Galaxy">Galaxy</a> people-carrier as well as its sister ships, the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Sharan" title="Volkswagen Sharan">VW Sharan</a> and <a href="/wiki/SEAT_Alhambra" title="SEAT Alhambra">SEAT Alhambra</a>. With the introduction of the third generation of the Galaxy, Ford has moved the production of the people-carrier to the Genk plant, with Volkswagen taking over sole ownership of the Setúbal facility.</p>
<p>In 2008, Ford acquired a majority stake in <a href="/wiki/Automobile_Craiova" title="Automobile Craiova">Automobile Craiova</a>, Romania. Starting 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Transit_Connect" title="Ford Transit Connect">Ford Transit Connect</a> was Ford's first model produced in <a href="/wiki/Craiova" title="Craiova">Craiova</a>, followed, in 2012, by low-capacity car engines and a new small class car, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_B-Max" title="Ford B-Max">B-Max</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Its 1959 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Anglia" title="Ford Anglia">Anglia</a> two-door saloon was one of the most quirky-looking small family cars in Europe at the time of its launch, but buyers soon became accustomed to its looks and it was hugely popular with British buyers in particular. It was still selling well when replaced by the more practical <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_(Europe)" title="Ford Escort (Europe)">Escort</a> in 1967.</p>
<p>The third incarnation of the Ford Escort was launched in 1980 and marked the company's move from rear-wheel drive saloons to front-wheel drive hatchbacks in the small family car sector.</p>
<p>The fourth generation Escort was produced from 1990 until 2000, although its successor – the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" title="Ford Focus (international)" class="mw-redirect">Focus</a> – had been on sale since 1998. On its launch, the Focus was arguably the most dramatic-looking and fine-handling small family cars on sale, and sold in huge volumes right up to the launch of the next generation Focus at the end of 2004.</p>
<p>The 1982 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Ford Sierra</a> – replacement for the long-running and massively popular <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cortina" title="Ford Cortina">Cortina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Taunus" title="Ford Taunus">Taunus</a> models – was a style-setter at the time of its launch. Its ultramodern aerodynamic design was a world away from a boxy, sharp-edged Cortina, and it was massively popular just about everywhere it was sold. A series of updates kept it looking relatively fresh until it was replaced by the front-wheel drive <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Mondeo</a> at the start of 1993.</p>
<p>The rise in popularity of small cars during the 1970s saw Ford enter the mini-car market in 1976 with its <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Fiesta</a> hatchback. Most of its production was concentrated at <a href="/wiki/Valencia,_Spain" title="Valencia, Spain" class="mw-redirect">Valencia</a> in Spain, and the Fiesta sold in huge figures from the very start. An update in 1983 and the launch of an all-new model in 1989 strengthened its position in the small car market.</p>
<p>On October 24, 2012, Ford announced that it would be closing its <a href="/wiki/Genk" title="Genk">Genk</a> assembly plant in eastern <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> by the end of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_Ford_Falcon_(FG_X)_XR6_Turbo_sedan_(23382738252).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/2014_Ford_Falcon_%28FG_X%29_XR6_Turbo_sedan_%2823382738252%29.jpg/220px-2014_Ford_Falcon_%28FG_X%29_XR6_Turbo_sedan_%2823382738252%29.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/2014_Ford_Falcon_%28FG_X%29_XR6_Turbo_sedan_%2823382738252%29.jpg/330px-2014_Ford_Falcon_%28FG_X%29_XR6_Turbo_sedan_%2823382738252%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/2014_Ford_Falcon_%28FG_X%29_XR6_Turbo_sedan_%2823382738252%29.jpg/440px-2014_Ford_Falcon_%28FG_X%29_XR6_Turbo_sedan_%2823382738252%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4080" data-file-height="2582" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_Ford_Falcon_(FG_X)_XR6_Turbo_sedan_(23382738252).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ford FG X Falcon (Australia)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg/220px-Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg/330px-Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg/440px-Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="648" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ford_stamping_plant_Geelong.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Ford stamping plant in Geelong, Australia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Australia and New Zealand, the popular <a href="/wiki/Ford_Falcon_(Australia)" title="Ford Falcon (Australia)">Ford Falcon</a> has long been considered the average family car and is considerably larger than the Mondeo, Ford's largest car sold in Europe. Between 1960 and 1972, the Falcon was based on a U.S. model of the same name, but since then has been entirely designed and manufactured in Australia, occasionally being manufactured in New Zealand. Like its <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> rival, the <a href="/wiki/Holden_Commodore" title="Holden Commodore">Holden Commodore</a>, the Falcon uses a rear wheel drive layout. High performance variants of the Falcon running locally built engines produce up to 362&#160;hp (270&#160;kW). A <a href="/wiki/Coup%C3%A9_utility" title="Coupé utility">ute</a> (short for "utility", known in the US as <a href="/wiki/Pickup_truck" title="Pickup truck">pickup truck</a>) version is also available with the same range of drivetrains. In addition, Ford Australia sells highly tuned limited-production Falcon sedans and <a href="/wiki/Pickup_truck" title="Pickup truck">utes</a> through its performance car division, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Performance_Vehicles" title="Ford Performance Vehicles">Ford Performance Vehicles</a>.</p>
<p>In Australia, the Commodore and Falcon have traditionally outsold all other cars and comprise over 20% of the new car market. In New Zealand, Ford was second in market share in the first eight months of 2006 with 14.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> More recently Ford has axed its Falcon-based LWB variant of its lineup– the Fairlane and LTD ranges, and announced that their Geelong engine manufacturing plant may be shut down from 2013. They have also announced local manufacturing of the Focus small car starting from 2011.</p>
<p>In Australia, the Laser was one of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_Australia" title="Ford Motor Company of Australia" class="mw-redirect">Ford Australia</a>'s most successful models, and was manufactured in Ford's <a href="/wiki/Homebush,_New_South_Wales" title="Homebush, New South Wales">Homebush</a> plant from 1981 until the plant's closure in September 1994. It outsold the Mazda 323, despite being almost identical to it, because the Laser was manufactured in Australia and Ford was perceived as a local brand.</p>
<p>In New Zealand, the Ford Laser and Telstar were assembled alongside the Mazda 323 and 626 until 1997, at the Vehicle Assemblers of New Zealand (VANZ) plant in <a href="/wiki/Wiri" title="Wiri">Wiri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Sierra" title="Ford Sierra">Sierra</a> wagon was also assembled in New Zealand, owing to the popularity of <a href="/wiki/Station_wagon" title="Station wagon">station wagons</a> in that market.</p>
<p>The scheduled closure of Ford's Australian manufacturing base in 2016 was confirmed in late May 2013. Headquartered in the Victorian suburb of Broadmeadows, the company had registered losses worth AU$600 million over the five years prior to the announcement. It was noted that the corporate fleet and government sales that account for two-thirds of large, local car sales in Australia are insufficient to keep Ford's products profitable and viable in Australia. The decision will affect 1200 Ford workers—over 600 employees in Geelong and more than 500 in Broadmeadows—who will lose their jobs by October 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_and_Southeast_Asia">East and Southeast Asia</span></h3>
<p>Ford formed its first passenger-vehicle joint venture in China in 2001, six years behind GM and more than a decade after VW. It has spent as of 2013 $4.9 billion to expand its lineup and double production capacity in China to 600,000 vehicles. This includes Ford's largest-ever factory complex in the southwestern city of Chongqing. Ford had 2.5% of the Chinese market in 2013, while VW controlled 14.5% and GM had 15.6%, according to consultant LMC Automotive. GM outsells Ford in China by more than six-to-one.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford's presence in Asia has traditionally been much smaller, confined to <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, Singapore, Hong Kong, the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, where Ford has had a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Ford_Lio_Ho_Motor" title="Ford Lio Ho Motor">Lio Ho</a> since the 1970s. Ford began assembly of cars in <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> in 1960, but withdrew from the country in 1976, and did not return until 1995, when it formed a joint venture with Mazda called Auto Alliance.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Now based in the Bo-win Sub District of the Sriracha District in <a href="/wiki/Chonburi_(city)" title="Chonburi (city)">Chonburi</a>, the factory still produces passenger automobiles. The factory built in 1941 in Singapore was shortly taken over by the Japanese during the war and was the site of a surrender of the British to the Japanese, at the <a href="/wiki/Old_Ford_Motor_Factory" title="Old Ford Motor Factory">factory site</a> which is now a national monument in Singapore.</p>
<p>On April 30, 2013, Ford Motor Co. launched their car and truck line in <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>. Previously, heavy importation taxes had stifled imported car purchases in Myanmar, but due to currency reform, lifting of previous import restrictions, and the abolishment of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_controls" title="Foreign exchange controls">shadow currency</a>, Myanmar's car market had grown in demand.<sup id="cite_ref-investvine_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investvine-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ford_of_Korea">Ford of Korea</span></h4>
<p>In 1967, Ford partnered with the South Korean company <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">Hyundai</a> and at the new factory in <a href="/wiki/Ulsan,_South_Korea" title="Ulsan, South Korea" class="mw-redirect">Ulsan, South Korea</a> built the European <a href="/wiki/Ford_Cortina" title="Ford Cortina">Ford Cortina</a> until 1974, when Hyundai introduced their all-new <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Pony" title="Hyundai Pony">Hyundai Pony</a> in 1975. Ford then developed a relationship with Korea's oldest car manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Kia_Motors" title="Kia Motors">Kia</a> which built vehicles co-engineered with <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a>, later selling the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Festiva" title="Ford Festiva">Ford Festiva</a> from 1988–1993, and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Festiva" title="Ford Festiva">Ford Aspire</a> from 1994–1997 for export to the United States. With the acquisition of a stake in Japanese manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> in 1979, Ford began selling Mazda's <a href="/wiki/Mazda_Familia" title="Mazda Familia">Familia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazda_Capella" title="Mazda Capella">Capella</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Laser" title="Ford Laser">Ford Laser</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Telstar" title="Ford Telstar">Telstar</a> throughout the region, replacing the European-sourced Escort and Cortina. Ford lost their Kia interest to Hyundai in 1998 during the <a href="/wiki/Asian_financial_crisis" title="Asian financial crisis" class="mw-redirect">Asian financial crisis</a>. Kia had declared bankruptcy in 1997; and in 1998, <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">Hyundai Motor Company</a> acquired 51% of the company, outbidding Ford which had owned an interest in Kia Motors since 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> After subsequent divestments,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Hyundai Motor Company owns less than 50% of the company but remains Kia's largest stakeholder.</p>
<p>Ford currently sells the Focus and Mondeo with diesel engines, plus the Mustang, Taurus, Escape, and Explorer, as well as the Lincoln MKS, MKZ, and MKC.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ford_of_Japan">Ford of Japan</span></h4>
<p>Ford established a manufacturing facility in the port city of Yokohama in February 1925, where Model T vehicles were assembled using imported <a href="/wiki/Knock-down_kit" title="Knock-down kit">knock-down kits</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> The factory subsequently produced 10,000 Model A's up to 1936. Production ceased in 1940 as a result of political tensions between Japan and the United States.</p>
<p>After World War II, Ford did not have a presence in Japan, as the Ford facility was appropriated by the Japanese Government until 1958, when property was returned as a possession of the Ford Motor Company and became a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mazda_facilities#R.26D" title="List of Mazda facilities">research and development location</a> for Ford partner <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a>. In 1979, Ford acquired a 24.5% ownership stake in Mazda, and in 1982 Ford and Mazda jointly established a sales channel to sell Ford products in Japan, including vehicles manufactured in North America, at a dealership called <i><a href="//ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E3%82%AA%E3%83%BC%E3%83%88%E3%83%A9%E3%83%9E" class="extiw" title="ja:オートラマ">Autorama</a> (Japanese)</i>. The Autorama sales channel was renamed Ford Sales of Japan in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Vehicles sold at <i>Autorama</i> locations were the North American assembled Ford Explorer, Probe (1989–1998), Mustang, Taurus (1989–1997), Thunderbird (1990–1993), Lincoln Continental, and Lincoln LS. Ford products manufactured in Europe that were sold in Japan were the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Ford Mondeo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ka" title="Ford Ka">Ka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus" title="Ford Focus">Focus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_C-Max" title="Ford C-Max">Focus C-MAX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Fiesta</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Galaxy" title="Ford Galaxy">Galaxy</a>. Mazda manufactured Ford vehicles in Japan and sold them as Fords at the Autorama locations. They were the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Telstar" title="Ford Telstar">Ford Telstar</a> (Mazda Capella), <a href="/wiki/Ford_Laser" title="Ford Laser">Laser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Festiva" title="Ford Festiva">Festiva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazda_Demio" title="Mazda Demio">Festiva Mini Wagon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ixion" title="Ford Ixion" class="mw-redirect">Ixion</a> (Mazda Premacy), <a href="/wiki/Ford_Freda" title="Ford Freda">Freda</a> (Mazda Bongo Friendee), <a href="/wiki/Ford_Spectron" title="Ford Spectron" class="mw-redirect">Spectron</a> (Mazda Bongo), and commercial trucks J80 and the J100 (Mazda Bongo truck).</p>
<p>Ford increased its shareholding in Mazda to 33.4% in 1996. Ford currently sells a small range of vehicles in Japan; as of October 2010, the Ford Mustang, Escape, Explorer (and Explorer truck), <a href="/wiki/Ford_Kuga" title="Ford Kuga">Ford Kuga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Navigator" title="Lincoln Navigator">Lincoln Navigator</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_MKX" title="Lincoln MKX">Lincoln MKX</a>, and more recently the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ecosport" title="Ford Ecosport" class="mw-redirect">Ford Ecosport</a> are available in Japan. Ford maintains a regional office in Minato, Tokyo, Japan.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_and_West_Asia">South and West Asia</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ford_India_Private_Limited" title="Ford India Private Limited">Ford India</a> began production in 1998 at <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a>, with its Ford Escort model, which was later replaced by the locally produced <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ikon" title="Ford Ikon">Ford Ikon</a> in 2001. It has since added the Fusion, Fiesta, Mondeo and Endeavour models to its product line.</p>
<p>On March 9, 2010, Ford Motor Co. launched its first made-for-India compact car. Starting at <span style="white-space:nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">₹</a>349,900</span>, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Figo" title="Ford Figo">Figo</a> was Ford's first car designed and priced for the mass Indian market.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> On July 28, 2011, Ford India signed a memorandum of understanding (MoU) with the State of <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> for the construction of an assembly and engine plant in <a href="/wiki/Sanand" title="Sanand">Sanand</a>, and planned to invest approximately <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1 billion</span> on a 460-acre site.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ford's market presence in the Middle East has traditionally been small, partly due to previous Arab boycotts of companies dealing with Israel. Ford and Lincoln vehicles are currently marketed in ten countries in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, Kuwait, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> are the biggest markets. Ford also established itself in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> in 1926, but faced an uphill battle during the 1950s due to the hostile nationalist business environment.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford's distributor in Saudi Arabia announced in February 2003 that it had sold 100,000 Ford and Lincoln vehicles since commencing sales in November 1986. Half of the Ford/Lincoln vehicles sold in that country were <a href="/wiki/Ford_Crown_Victoria" title="Ford Crown Victoria">Ford Crown Victorias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, Ford sold 30,000 units in the region, falling far short of <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>' 88,852 units and <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan Motors</a>' 75,000 units.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span></h3>
<p>During much of the 20th century, Ford faced protectionist government measures in South America, with the result that it built different models in different countries, without particular regard to rationalization or <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_scale" title="Economy of scale" class="mw-redirect">economy of scale</a> inherent to producing and sharing similar vehicles between the nations. In many cases, new vehicles in a country were based on those of the other manufacturers it had entered into production agreements with, or whose factories it had acquired. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Corcel" title="Ford Corcel">Corcel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Del_Rey" title="Ford Del Rey">Del Rey</a> in Brazil were originally based on <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> vehicles.</p>
<p>In 1987, <a href="/wiki/Ford_do_Brasil" title="Ford do Brasil" class="mw-redirect">Ford of Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company_of_Argentina" title="Ford Motor Company of Argentina" class="mw-redirect">Ford of Argentina</a> merged their operations with the Brazilian and Argentine operations of <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a>, forming a new joint-venture company called <a href="/wiki/Autolatina" title="Autolatina">Autolatina</a> with a shared model range. Sales figures and profitability were disappointing, and Autolatina was dissolved in 1995. With the advent of <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a>, the regional common market, Ford was finally able to rationalize its product line-ups in those countries. Consequently, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Ford Fiesta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ford_EcoSport" title="Ford EcoSport">Ford EcoSport</a> are only built in Brazil, and the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_(international)" title="Ford Focus (international)" class="mw-redirect">Ford Focus</a> only built in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, with each plant exporting in large volumes to the neighboring countries. Models like the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo" title="Ford Mondeo">Ford Mondeo</a> from Europe could now be imported completely built up. Ford of Brazil produces a pick-up truck version of the Fiesta, the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Courier" title="Ford Courier">Courier</a>, which is also produced in South Africa as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Bantam" title="Ford Bantam">Ford Bantam</a> in <a href="/wiki/Driving_on_the_left_or_right" title="Driving on the left or right" class="mw-redirect">right hand drive</a> versions.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span></h3>
<p>In Africa, Ford's market presence has traditionally been strongest in South Africa and neighbouring countries, with only trucks being sold elsewhere on the continent. Ford in South Africa began by importing kits from Canada to be assembled at its Port Elizabeth facility. Later Ford sourced its models from the UK and Australia, with local versions of the Ford Cortina including the XR6, with a 3.0 V6 engine, and a <a href="/wiki/Ford_P100" title="Ford P100">Cortina-based 'bakkie' or pick-up</a>, which was exported to the UK. In the mid-1980s Ford merged with a rival company, owned by <a href="/wiki/Anglo_American_plc" title="Anglo American plc">Anglo American</a>, to form the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Motor_Corporation" title="South African Motor Corporation" class="mw-redirect">South African Motor Corporation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Samcor" title="Samcor">Samcor</a>).</p>
<p>Following international condemnation of <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>, Ford divested from South Africa in 1988, and sold its stake in Samcor, although it licensed the use of its brand name to the company. Samcor began to assemble Mazdas as well, which affected its product line-up, and saw the European Fords like the Escort and Sierra replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a>-based Laser and <a href="/wiki/Ford_Telstar" title="Ford Telstar">Telstar</a>. Ford bought a 45 per cent stake in <a href="/wiki/Samcor" title="Samcor">Samcor</a> following the demise of apartheid in 1994, and this later became, once again, a wholly owned subsidiary, the Ford Motor Company of Southern Africa. Ford now sells a local sedan version of the Fiesta (also built in India and Mexico), and the Focus. The Falcon model from Australia was also sold in South Africa, but was dropped in 2003, while the Mondeo, after briefly being assembled locally, was dropped in 2005. The Mondeo has since been reintroduced, but badged as the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fusion_(Americas)" title="Ford Fusion (Americas)">Fusion</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Automobiles">Automobiles</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ford_vehicles" title="List of Ford vehicles">List of Ford vehicles</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lincoln_vehicles" title="List of Lincoln vehicles">List of Lincoln vehicles</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Mercury_vehicles" title="List of Mercury vehicles">List of Mercury vehicles</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2013_Lincoln_MKS_--_2012_DC.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/2013_Lincoln_MKS_--_2012_DC.JPG/220px-2013_Lincoln_MKS_--_2012_DC.JPG" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/2013_Lincoln_MKS_--_2012_DC.JPG/330px-2013_Lincoln_MKS_--_2012_DC.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/2013_Lincoln_MKS_--_2012_DC.JPG/440px-2013_Lincoln_MKS_--_2012_DC.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2332" data-file-height="1464" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2013_Lincoln_MKS_--_2012_DC.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 2013 model year <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_MKS" title="Lincoln MKS">Lincoln MKS</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ford Motor Company sells a broad range of automobiles under the Ford marque worldwide, and an additional range of luxury automobiles under the <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_(automobile)" title="Lincoln (automobile)" class="mw-redirect">Lincoln</a> marque in the United States. The company has sold vehicles under a number of other marques during its history. The <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(automobile)" title="Mercury (automobile)">Mercury</a> brand was introduced by Ford in 1939, continuing in production until 2011 when poor sales led to its discontinuation.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1958, Ford introduced the <a href="/wiki/Edsel" title="Edsel">Edsel</a> brand, but poor sales led to its discontinuation in 1960. In 1985, the <a href="/wiki/Merkur" title="Merkur">Merkur</a> brand was introduced in the United States to market products produced by Ford of Europe; it was discontinued in 1989.</p>
<p>Ford acquired the British sports car maker <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a> in 1989, later selling it on March 12, 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> although retaining an 8% stake.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford purchased <a href="/wiki/Volvo_Cars" title="Volvo Cars">Volvo Cars</a> of Sweden in 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> selling it to <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang_Geely_Holding_Group" title="Zhejiang Geely Holding Group" class="mw-redirect">Zhejiang Geely Holding Group</a> in 2010. In November 2008, it reduced its 33.4% <a href="/wiki/Controlling_interest" title="Controlling interest">controlling interest</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mazda" title="Mazda">Mazda</a> of Japan to a 13.4% non-controlling interest.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> On November 18, 2010, Ford reduced their stake further to just 3%, citing the reduction of ownership would allow greater flexibility to pursue growth in emerging markets. Ford and Mazda remain strategic partners through exchanges of technological information and joint ventures, including an American joint venture plant in Flat Rock, Michigan called <a href="/wiki/Auto_Alliance" title="Auto Alliance" class="mw-redirect">Auto Alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Ford sold the United Kingdom-based <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Cars" title="Jaguar Cars">Jaguar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Land_Rover" title="Land Rover">Land Rover</a> companies and brands to <a href="/wiki/Tata_Motors" title="Tata Motors">Tata Motors</a> of India in March 2008.</p>
